| **THE PROVISIONS OF THIS ENDORSEMENT FORMALLY INCLUDE THE MANAGING MEMBERS OF BLUE KETTLE FOOD SERVICE, LLC WITHIN THE SCOPE OF THE WORKERS COMPENSATION COVERAGE. BY DEFAULT, MEMBERS OF A LIMITED LIABILITY COMPANY MAY BE EXCLUDED FROM STATUTORY BENEFITS IN CERTAIN JURISDICTIONS UNLESS A SPECIFIC ELECTION IS MADE TO INCLUDE THEM. THIS DOCUMENT SERVES AS THE FORMAL ELECTION OF INCLUSION.** <br><br> Remuneration for included members is subject to the statutory minimum and maximum payroll constraints established by the respective state rating bureaus. For premium calculation purposes, the remuneration of each included member will be capped at the state-specific maximum, regardless of their actual earnings. Conversely, if a member's actual earnings fall below the state minimum, the minimum payroll amount will be utilized. <br><br> The payroll for the included members must be assigned to the classification code that most accurately reflects their primary occupational duties. If a member performs duties that span multiple classifications, their entire remuneration will be assigned to the highest-rated classification code applicable to their activities, unless meticulous time records are maintained. <br><br> The named insured must provide a complete roster of all managing members at the inception of the policy period and notify the carrier of any changes in membership status. The election to include members remains in effect for the duration of the policy period and any subsequent renewals unless formally revoked in writing by the named insured. <br><br> References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include MA class code 5190 only for the state and operation shown in the information page. <br><br> Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions. <br><br> If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state. | The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries. <br><br> Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement. <br><br> A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued. <br><br> Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records. <br><br> When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together. <br><br> **SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT** <br><br> The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Electrical wiring within buildings assigned to class code 5190 in MA. <br><br> The remuneration entry of $77,560 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy. <br><br> Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state. <br><br> If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules. <br><br> **SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS** <br><br> State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet. <br><br> A classification shown on a schedule is not a warranty that all operations at the insured location are limited to that class. <br><br> Officer, partner, member, volunteer, leased-worker, and subcontractor treatment is determined by the attached endorsements and the applicable state rules. <br><br> Certificates from subcontractors must be available for audit and must identify the period of work, covered operations, and limits carried by the subcontractor. |

Waiver of Recovery Endorsement 4

                         WAIVER OF RECOVERY ENDORSEMENT

Endorsement No. WC-EN-008                                   Effective 08/01/2026

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ITEM,STATE / CLASS
WC-0008,VT / 5606
CLASSIFICATION,PAYROLL / RATE
Contractor executive supervisor,$127,460 / 6.22
PREMIUM,FORM
$7,928,WC 00 00 01 A 04 21
ENDORSEMENT,EFFECTIVE DATE
WC-EN-008,08/01/2026
MATERIALITY,
Material,
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

THIS ENDORSEMENT, BEARING THE NUMBER WC-EN-001 AND EFFECTIVE 01/01/2026, RESTRICTS THE ABILITY OF ARGENT BIRCH EMPLOYERS TO PURSUE RECOVERY AGAINST THIRD PARTIES. THE CARRIER RELINQUISHES THE RIGHT TO SEEK REIMBURSEMENT FOR STATUTORY BENEFITS PAID TO AN INJURED EMPLOYEE FROM THE SPECIFIC ENTITIES DESIGNATED IN THE SCHEDULE ATTACHED TO THIS ENDORSEMENT.

The waiver applies specifically to the operations and locations detailed in the classification schedule, provided the named insured has executed a written contract requiring such a waiver prior to the occurrence of the occupational injury. The waiver does not apply if the third party is solely responsible for the injury due to gross negligence or intentional misconduct.

The application of this waiver requires the payment of an additional premium charge, which is calculated as a percentage of the manual premium generated by the operations subject to the waiver. This additional premium is subject to the experience modification factor and is included in the final audited premium calculation.

Blue Kettle Food Service, LLC must maintain copies of all contracts requiring a waiver of recovery and present them during the premium audit. The carrier retains the right to review these contracts to verify the applicability of the waiver and ensure the proper calculation of the associated premium charges.

References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include VT class code 5606 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.

Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.

If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state.

The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.


Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.

A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.

Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.

When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.

SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT

The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Contractor executive supervisor assigned to class code 5606 in VT.

The remuneration entry of $127,460 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.

Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.

If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.

SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS

State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet.

A classification shown on a schedule is not a warranty that all operations at the insured location are limited to that class.

Officer, partner, member, volunteer, leased-worker, and subcontractor treatment is determined by the attached endorsements and the applicable state rules.

Certificates from subcontractors must be available for audit and must identify the period of work, covered operations, and limits carried by the subcontractor.

---

### **LIMITED LIABILITY COMPANY MEMBER INCLUSION**

Endorsement No. WC-EN-012 <span style="float: right;">Effective 12/01/2026</span>

| **ITEM**<br>**WC-0012** | **STATE / CLASS**<br>**MA / 5190** |
| :--- | :--- |
| **CLASSIFICATION**<br>**Electrical wiring within buildings** | **PAYROLL / RATE**<br>**$171,391 / 0.27** |
| **PREMIUM**<br>**$462** | **FORM**<br>**WC 04 03 06 04 21** |
| **ENDORSEMENT**<br>**WC-EN-012** | **EFFECTIVE DATE**<br>**12/01/2026** |
| **MATERIALITY**<br>**No Material Change** | |

---

<table border="0" width="100%">
<tr>
<td width="50%" valign="top" style="padding-right: 20px;">

**THE PROVISIONS OF THIS ENDORSEMENT FORMALLY INCLUDE THE MANAGING MEMBERS OF BLUE KETTLE FOOD SERVICE, LLC WITHIN THE SCOPE OF THE WORKERS COMPENSATION COVERAGE. BY DEFAULT, MEMBERS OF A LIMITED LIABILITY COMPANY MAY BE EXCLUDED FROM STATUTORY BENEFITS IN CERTAIN JURISDICTIONS UNLESS A SPECIFIC ELECTION IS MADE TO INCLUDE THEM. THIS DOCUMENT SERVES AS THE FORMAL ELECTION OF INCLUSION.**

Remuneration for included members is subject to the statutory minimum and maximum payroll constraints established by the respective state rating bureaus. For premium calculation purposes, the remuneration of each included member will be capped at the state-specific maximum, regardless of their actual earnings. Conversely, if a member's actual earnings fall below the state minimum, the minimum payroll amount will be utilized.

The payroll for the included members must be assigned to the classification code that most accurately reflects their primary occupational duties. If a member performs duties that span multiple classifications, their entire remuneration will be assigned to the highest-rated classification code applicable to their activities, unless meticulous time records are maintained.

The named insured must provide a complete roster of all managing members at the inception of the policy period and notify the carrier of any changes in membership status. The election to include members remains in effect for the duration of the policy period and any subsequent renewals unless formally revoked in writing by the named insured.

References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include MA class code 5190 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.

Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.

If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state.

</td>
<td width="50%" valign="top" style="padding-left: 20px; border-left: 1px solid #ddd;">

The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.

Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.

A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.

Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.

When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.

**SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT**

The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Electrical wiring within buildings assigned to class code 5190 in MA.

The remuneration entry of $171,391 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.

Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.

If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.

**SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS**

State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet.

A classification shown on a schedule is not a warranty that all operations at the insured location are limited to that class.

Officer, partner, member, volunteer, leased-worker, and subcontractor treatment is determined by the attached endorsements and the applicable state rules.

Certificates from subcontractors must be available for audit and must identify the period of work, covered operations, and limits carried by the subcontractor.

</td>
</tr>
</table>

---
Authorized Representative <span style="float: right; margin-right: 300px;">Countersignature Date</span>

Electrical Operations Safety Endorsement 9

YW700400
04/01/2026 - 04/01/2027

ELECTRICAL OPERATIONS SAFETY ENDORSEMENT

Endorsement No. WC-EN-017                                                                    Effective 05/01/2026

ITEM,STATE / CLASS
WC-0017,CT / 8810
CLASSIFICATION,PAYROLL / RATE
Clerical office employees,$234,108 / 2.86
PREMIUM,FORM
$6,695,WC 04 03 06 01 15
ENDORSEMENT,EFFECTIVE DATE
WC-EN-017,05/01/2026
MATERIALITY,
No Material Change,

EFFECTIVE 04/01/2026, THIS ENDORSEMENT APPLIES SPECIFICALLY TO OPERATIONS CLASSIFIED UNDER CODE 5190 FOR ELECTRICAL WIRING WITHIN BUILDINGS. DUE TO THE INHERENT HAZARDS ASSOCIATED WITH THESE ACTIVITIES, ARGENT BIRCH EMPLOYERS REQUIRES THE IMPLEMENTATION OF SPECIFIC SAFETY PROTOCOLS TO MITIGATE THE RISK OF OCCUPATIONAL INJURIES. THIS ENDORSEMENT MODIFIES THE GENERAL POLICY CONDITIONS REGARDING EMPLOYER DUTIES.

Blue Kettle Food Service, LLC must ensure that all personnel engaged in electrical wiring activities maintain the appropriate state licensure and certifications required by the Commonwealth of Massachusetts. The named insured must verify the credentials of all employees and independent contractors prior to their commencement of electrical work at any job site.

The employer must provide and mandate the use of personal protective equipment, including arc flash suits, insulated gloves, and safety eyewear, for all individuals performing tasks under class code 5190. Furthermore, the named insured must implement a comprehensive lockout/tagout program to prevent the accidental energization of electrical circuits during maintenance or installation procedures.

Failure to adhere to the safety protocols outlined in this endorsement may result in the application of a safety penalty surcharge during the final premium audit. Argent Birch Employers retains the right to conduct unannounced safety inspections at any active job site to verify compliance with these requirements.

References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include CT class code 8810 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.

Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.

If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state.

The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.

Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.

A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.

Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.

When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.

SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT

The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Clerical office employees assigned to class code 8810 in CT.

The remuneration entry of $234,108 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.

Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.

If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.

SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS

State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet.

A classification shown on a schedule is not a warranty that all operations at the insured location are limited to that class.

Officer, partner, member, volunteer, leased-worker, and subcontractor treatment is determined by the attached endorsements and the applicable state rules.

Certificates from subcontractors must be available for audit and must identify the period of work, covered operations, and limits carried by the subcontractor.

___________________________________________________                  ___________________________________________________
Authorized Representative                                            Countersignature Date

Blue Kettle Food Service, LLC                                                                            WC 04 03 06

| **ARGENT BIRCH EMPLOYERS REQUIRES THE MAINTENANCE OF PRECISE PAYROLL RECORDS FOR ALL INDIVIDUALS ENGAGED BY BLUE KETTLE FOOD SERVICE, LLC. THIS NOTIFICATION SERVES AS A FORMAL REMINDER OF THE RECORDKEEPING OBLIGATIONS ESSENTIAL FOR THE FINAL PREMIUM DETERMINATION. ACCURATE DOCUMENTATION IS CRITICAL FOR THE PROPER ASSIGNMENT OF REMUNERATION TO THE SCHEDULED CLASSIFICATION CODES, INCLUDING 8810, 8017, 8742, AND 5190.**<br><br>The required documentation includes, but is not limited to, state and federal tax summaries, individual employee earnings records, general ledgers, cash disbursement journals, and certificates of insurance for all independent contractors utilized during the policy period. The records must clearly indicate the specific duties performed by each individual and the state in which those duties were executed.<br><br>Particular attention must be given to the segregation of payroll for employees who perform duties that span multiple classification codes. The named insured must maintain verifiable daily time records detailing the hours dedicated to each specific occupational task. In the absence of such detailed records, the entire remuneration for the employee will be assigned to the highest-rated classification code applicable to their duties.<br><br>Failure to provide adequate documentation during the final audit may result in the application of penalty provisions, including the assignment of undocumented remuneration to the highest-rated classification code or the implementation of an audit noncompliance charge. The named insured must ensure that all relevant records are readily accessible for review by the carrier's audit personnel.<br><br>References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include RI class code 9082 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.<br><br>Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.<br><br>If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state. | The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.<br><br>Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.<br><br>A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.<br><br>Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.<br><br>When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.<br><br>**SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT**<br><br>The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Restaurant NOC assigned to class code 9082 in RI.<br><br>The remuneration entry of $277,752 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.<br><br>Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.<br><br>If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.<br><br>**SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS**<br><br>State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet.<br><br>A classification shown on a schedule is not a warranty that all operations at the insured location are limited to that class.<br><br>Officer, partner, member, volunteer, leased-worker, and subcontractor treatment is determined by the attached endorsements and the applicable state rules.<br><br>Certificates from subcontractors must be available for audit and must identify the period of work, covered operations, and limits carried by the subcontractor. |

| **THE ESTIMATED PREMIUM FOR THIS POLICY IS DERIVED FROM THE ANTICIPATED ANNUAL REMUNERATION DISTRIBUTED ACROSS THE DESIGNATED CLASSIFICATION CODES. ALL PREMIUM CALCULATIONS UTILIZE A BASIS OF PAYROLL PER $100 REMUNERATION. FOR OPERATIONS WITHIN CONNECTICUT, CLASS CODE 8810 DESIGNATES CLERICAL OFFICE EMPLOYEES, REFLECTING AN ESTIMATED ANNUAL PAYROLL OF $45,136 AND A MANUAL RATE OF 0.42, GENERATING AN ESTIMATED PREMIUM OF $189. THIS CLASSIFICATION IS CONSIDERED THE GOVERNING CLASS FOR THE CONNECTICUT LOCATIONS.**<br><br>Additionally, Connecticut operations include class code 8017 for Retail store - all employees. This secondary classification captures an estimated annual payroll of $54,124 at a manual rate of 0.74, resulting in an estimated premium of $400. The named insured must ensure that employee duties strictly align with the parameters of these classifications to avoid retroactive premium adjustments during the final audit process.<br><br>Operations within Massachusetts are categorized under separate classification codes reflecting distinct occupational hazards. Class code 8742 applies to Outside salespersons, with an anticipated annual payroll of $70,826. Applying the manual rate of 0.18 yields an estimated premium of $127. Furthermore, class code 5190 captures activities related to Electrical wiring within buildings, showing an estimated remuneration of $77,560 at a manual rate of 2.86, which generates an estimated premium of $2,218.<br><br>The total estimated premium is provisional and serves as the basis for initial billing. The final premium will be determined upon the completion of a comprehensive payroll audit. The experience modification factor of 1.04 is applied to the aggregate manual premium across all scheduled states and classifications. Any material change in operations, including the introduction of new job duties or expansion into additional states, must be reported to Argent Birch Employers immediately.<br><br>References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include CT class code 8017 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.<br><br>Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.<br><br>If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state. | The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.<br><br>Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.<br><br>A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.<br><br>Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.<br><br>When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.<br><br>**SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT**<br><br>The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Retail store - all employees assigned to class code 8017 in CT.<br><br>The remuneration entry of $54,124 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.<br><br>Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.<br><br>If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.<br><br>**SECTION B - | **THIS ENDORSEMENT ESTABLISHES A FRAMEWORK FOR PROVIDING STATUTORY BENEFITS TO INDIVIDUALS WHO MAY NOT FALL WITHIN THE MANDATORY SCOPE OF THE APPLICABLE STATE WORKERS COMPENSATION STATUTES. BLUE KETTLE FOOD SERVICE, LLC MAY ELECT TO OFFER THESE BENEFITS TO EXEMPT EMPLOYEES, INDEPENDENT CONTRACTORS, OR VOLUNTEERS, PROVIDED SUCH INDIVIDUALS SUSTAIN AN OCCUPATIONAL INJURY WHILE PERFORMING DUTIES DIRECTLY RELATED TO THE SCHEDULED OPERATIONS.**<br><br>The provision of voluntary benefits is contingent upon the injured individual executing a full release of liability in favor of the named insured and Argent Birch Employers. The injured party must waive any common law rights to pursue civil litigation regarding the workplace incident. If the individual rejects the voluntary benefits and initiates a civil action, the provisions of this endorsement immediately cease to apply to that specific incident.<br><br>Remuneration for individuals covered under this voluntary arrangement must be included in the payroll records and assigned to the classification code that most accurately reflects their occupational duties. The manual rates, experience modification factor, and schedule rating adjustments will be applied to this remuneration in the same manner as mandatory payroll.<br><br>Argent Birch Employers will administer the voluntary benefits in accordance with the statutory schedules of the state where the injury occurred, as if the injured individual were a mandatory employee. [COLUMN 1]

EMPLOYERS LIABILITY PROVISIONS ADDRESS THE FINANCIAL CONSEQUENCES OF WORKPLACE INJURIES NOT STRICTLY RESOLVED THROUGH STATUTORY WORKERS COMPENSATION FRAMEWORKS. THIS SECTION APPLIES TO BODILY INJURY BY ACCIDENT OR BODILY INJURY BY DISEASE ARISING OUT OF AND IN THE COURSE OF THE INJURED EMPLOYEE'S EMPLOYMENT BY BLUE KETTLE FOOD SERVICE, LLC. THE INJURY MUST OCCUR DURING THE POLICY PERIOD AND WITHIN THE DESIGNATED COVERAGE TERRITORIES.

The insured entity must immediately forward any demands, notices, summonses, or legal papers received in connection with a claim or suit. Argent Birch Employers will manage the legal response to such actions, utilizing appointed counsel to navigate the complexities of the litigation. The carrier retains the exclusive authority to investigate, negotiate, and settle any claim or suit as deemed appropriate.

Coverage under this section is subject to specific limitations regarding the maximum financial responsibility of the carrier. These limitations apply separately to bodily injury by accident, bodily injury by disease per employee, and an aggregate limit for bodily injury by disease. The application of the experience modification factor does not alter these established limitations.

Exclusions apply to liability assumed under a contract, punitive damages, and injuries sustained by employees employed in violation of the law with the actual knowledge of the named insured. Furthermore, this section does not apply to any obligation imposed by a workers compensation, occupational disease, unemployment compensation, or disability benefits law.

References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include MA class code 5190 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.

Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.

If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state.

[COLUMN 2]

The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.

Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.

A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.

Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.

When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.

SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT
The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Electrical wiring within buildings assigned to class code 5190 in MA.

The remuneration entry of $77,560 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.

Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.

If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.

SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS
State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet.

| :--- | :--- |
| **BRINDLE COAST COVERAGE GROUP, OPERATING UNDER PRODUCER CODE PX-73916, RECEIVES COMPENSATION FOR THE PLACEMENT AND SERVICING OF THIS POLICY. THIS DISCLOSURE OUTLINES THE NATURE OF THE FINANCIAL ARRANGEMENT BETWEEN ARGENT BIRCH EMPLOYERS AND THE DESIGNATED PRODUCER. THE COMPENSATION IS INCORPORATED INTO THE OVERALL PREMIUM STRUCTURE AND DOES NOT REPRESENT AN ADDITIONAL FEE CHARGED DIRECTLY TO THE NAMED INSURED.** | Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement. |
| | |
| The compensation may include base commissions calculated as a percentage of the final audited premium. The commission rate varies depending on the line of business, the state of operation, and the specific contractual agreement between the carrier and the producer. The base commission compensates the producer for activities such as risk assessment, policy negotiation, and ongoing customer service. | A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued. |
| | |
| In addition to base commissions, Brindle Coast Coverage Group may be eligible for contingent compensation based on the aggregate performance of a portfolio of policies placed with Argent Birch Employers. Contingent compensation is typically tied to metrics such as profitability, retention rates, and premium volume. This variable compensation is not guaranteed and is calculated retrospectively. | Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records. |
| | |

Furthermore, class code 5190 captures activities related to Electrical wiring within buildings, showing an estimated remuneration of $77,560 at a manual rate of 2.86, which generates an estimated premium of $2,218. <br><br> The total estimated premium is provisional and serves as the basis for initial billing. The final premium will be determined upon the completion of a comprehensive payroll audit. The experience modification factor of 1.04 is applied to the aggregate manual premium across all scheduled states and classifications. Any material change in operations, including the introduction of new job duties or expansion into additional states, must be reported to Argent Birch Employers immediately. <br><br> References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include NH class code 9015 only for the state and operation shown in the information page. <br><br> Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions. <br><br> If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state. | The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries. <br><br> Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement. <br><br> A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued. <br><br> Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records. <br><br> When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together. <br><br> **SECTION A - **ADMINISTRATIVE PROVISIONS CONCERNING OPERATIONS IN CONNECTICUT ARE ALTERED BY THIS ENDORSEMENT TO ALIGN WITH THE REGULATORY FRAMEWORK OF THE STATE. THIS DOCUMENT APPLIES TO THE OCCUPATIONAL EXPOSURES CATEGORIZED UNDER CLASS CODES 8810 AND 8017. THE PROVISIONS OF THIS ENDORSEMENT TAKE PRECEDENCE OVER ANY GENERAL POLICY CONDITIONS THAT CONFLICT WITH CONNECTICUT STATUTES.**

The named insured must designate an authorized medical provider network or establish a preferred provider arrangement in accordance with the guidelines set forth by the Connecticut Workers' Compensation Commission. Employees sustaining occupational injuries must be directed to utilize the designated medical providers, subject to the exceptions and patient rights outlined in the state regulations.

Cancellation and nonrenewal notices will be mailed to the primary address of the named insured at 914 Millrace Parkway, Worcester, MA 01608, via certified mail or another verifiable delivery method. The carrier must adhere to the specific notice periods mandated by Connecticut law, which vary depending on the reason for the policy termination.

The administration of claims, including the calculation of average weekly wages and the determination of disability duration, will be governed by the Connecticut Workers' Compensation Act. Argent Birch Employers will facilitate the payment of statutory benefits, including medical expenses, temporary total disability, and permanent partial disability, in accordance with the schedules established by the Commission.

References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include VT class code 5606 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.

Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.

If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state.

The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.

</div>
<div style="flex: 1;">

Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.

A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.

Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.

When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.

**SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT**

The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Contractor executive supervisor assigned to class code 5606 in VT.

The remuneration entry of $127,460 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.

Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.

If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.

**SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS**

| **THIS NOTICE PROVIDES ADMINISTRATIVE DETAILS REGARDING THE APPLICATION OF THE EXPERIENCE MODIFICATION FACTOR TO POLICY NUMBER YW700400. THE EXPERIENCE MODIFICATION FACTOR IS A STATISTICAL ADJUSTMENT CALCULATED BY THE RELEVANT RATING BUREAU, REFLECTING THE HISTORICAL CLAIM FREQUENCY AND SEVERITY OF BLUE KETTLE FOOD SERVICE, LLC COMPARED TO THE INDUSTRY AVERAGE. FOR THE CURRENT POLICY PERIOD, THE CALCULATED EXPERIENCE MODIFICATION FACTOR STANDS AT 1.04.** | The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries. |
| The experience modification factor and schedule rating entry apply to the policy as a whole unless a state-specific endorsement provides otherwise. This factor is multiplied by the aggregate manual premium generated by the classification codes across all scheduled states. A factor greater than 1.00 indicates a historical loss experience that exceeds the expected average, resulting in an upward adjustment to the premium. | Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement. |
| The named insured has the right to review the underlying loss data and payroll figures used in the calculation of the experience modification factor. Any discrepancies or errors in the historical data must be reported to the rating bureau for correction. Argent Birch Employers does not calculate the factor and is bound by the promulgation issued by the authorized rating organization. | A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued. |
| Changes to the experience modification factor may occur during the policy period due to revised loss data, changes in ownership, or the combination of affiliated entities. If a revised factor is issued, the carrier will endorse the policy and adjust the estimated premium accordingly. The named insured is responsible for any additional premium resulting from an upward revision of the factor. | Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records. |
| References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include RI class code 9082 only for the state and operation shown in the information page. | When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together. |
| Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions. | **SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT** |
| If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state. | The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Restaurant NOC assigned to class code 9082 in RI. |
| | The remuneration entry of $184,316 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy. |
| | Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state. |
| | If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules. |
| | **SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS** |
| | State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet. |
| | A classification shown on a schedule is not a warranty that all operations at the insured location are limited to that class. |
| | Officer, partner, member, volunteer, leased-worker, and subcontractor treatment is determined by the attached endorsements and the applicable state rules. |
| | Certificates from subcontractors must be available for audit and must identify the period of work, covered operations, and limits carried by the subcontractor. |

| **BRINDLE COAST COVERAGE GROUP, OPERATING UNDER PRODUCER CODE PX-73916, RECEIVES COMPENSATION FOR THE PLACEMENT AND SERVICING OF THIS POLICY. THIS DISCLOSURE OUTLINES THE NATURE OF THE FINANCIAL ARRANGEMENT BETWEEN ARGENT BIRCH EMPLOYERS AND THE DESIGNATED PRODUCER. THE COMPENSATION IS INCORPORATED INTO THE OVERALL PREMIUM STRUCTURE AND DOES NOT REPRESENT AN ADDITIONAL FEE CHARGED DIRECTLY TO THE NAMED INSURED.** | Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement. |
| The compensation may include base commissions calculated as a percentage of the final audited premium. The commission rate varies depending on the line of business, the state of operation, and the specific contractual agreement between the carrier and the producer. The base commission compensates the producer for activities such as risk assessment, policy negotiation, and ongoing customer service. | A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued. |
| In addition to base commissions, Brindle Coast Coverage Group may be eligible for contingent compensation based on the aggregate performance of a portfolio of policies placed with Argent Birch Employers. Contingent compensation is typically tied to metrics such as profitability, retention rates, and premium volume. This variable compensation is not guaranteed and is calculated retrospectively. | Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records. |
| Blue Kettle Food Service, LLC may request detailed information regarding the specific compensation associated with policy number YW700400. Requests for detailed compensation disclosures must be submitted in writing to the carrier. Argent Birch Employers is committed to maintaining transparency regarding producer compensation arrangements. | When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together. <br><br> **SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT** |

                                   CLASSIFICATION AND PREMIUM SCHEDULE

WC 00 00 00 C policy form                                                        Policy No. YW700400

ITEM,STATE / CLASS
WC-0017,CT / 8810
CLASSIFICATION,PAYROLL / RATE
Clerical office employees,"$234,108 / 2.86"
PREMIUM,FORM
"$6,695",WC 04 03 06 01 15

THE ESTIMATED PREMIUM FOR THIS POLICY IS DERIVED FROM THE ANTICIPATED ANNUAL REMUNERATION DISTRIBUTED ACROSS THE DESIGNATED CLASSIFICATION CODES. ALL PREMIUM CALCULATIONS UTILIZE A BASIS OF PAYROLL PER $100 REMUNERATION. FOR OPERATIONS WITHIN CONNECTICUT, CLASS CODE 8810 DESIGNATES CLERICAL OFFICE EMPLOYEES, REFLECTING AN ESTIMATED ANNUAL PAYROLL OF $45,136 AND A MANUAL RATE OF 0.42, GENERATING AN ESTIMATED PREMIUM OF $189. THIS CLASSIFICATION IS CONSIDERED THE GOVERNING CLASS FOR THE CONNECTICUT LOCATIONS.

Additionally, Connecticut operations include class code 8017 for Retail store - all employees. This secondary classification captures an estimated annual payroll of $54,124 at a manual rate of 0.74, resulting in an estimated premium of $400. The named insured must ensure that employee duties strictly align with the parameters of these classifications to avoid retroactive premium adjustments during the final audit process.

Operations within Massachusetts are categorized under separate classification codes reflecting distinct occupational hazards. Class code 8742 applies to Outside salespersons, with an anticipated annual payroll of $70,826. Applying the manual rate of 0.18 yields an estimated premium of $127. Furthermore, class code 5190 captures activities related to Electrical wiring within buildings, showing an estimated remuneration of $77,560 at a manual rate of 2.86, which generates an estimated premium of $2,218.

The total estimated premium is provisional and serves as the basis for initial billing. The final premium will be determined upon the completion of a comprehensive payroll audit. The experience modification factor of 1.04 is applied to the aggregate manual premium across all scheduled states and classifications. Any material change in operations, including the introduction of new job duties or expansion into additional states, must be reported to Argent Birch Employers immediately.

References to classification, remuneration, and rating basis include CT class code 8810 only for the state and operation shown in the information page.

Headings are included for ease of reading and do not alter statutory benefits, employers liability limits, audit rights, or state amendatory provisions.

If a state endorsement and a general condition address the same subject, the state-specific endorsement controls for the affected state.

The insured should retain payroll journals, tax filings, subcontractor certificates, job-duty records, and officer status records used to support the classification entries.

Classification summaries on one page do not replace the information page, payroll schedule, endorsement schedule, or premium audit statement.

A certificate, binder note, invoice, or producer correspondence item does not amend a payroll or class-code entry unless an endorsement is issued.

Final premium may require allocation of remuneration by state, governing class, officer status, overtime treatment, and subcontracted work records.

When a class code appears on multiple schedules, the state, item identifier, and effective date should be used to read the entries together.

SECTION A - RECORDS AND AUDIT

The insured must keep payroll journals, tax filings, job-duty records, and contract labor records for Clerical office employees assigned to class code 8810 in CT.

The remuneration entry of $234,108 is an estimate for rating purposes and may be revised after audit without changing the coverage afforded by the policy.

Separate records are required when an employee performs duties that may fall under more than one classification or more than one covered state.

If adequate records are not available, remuneration may be assigned to the highest rated applicable classification permitted by the rating rules.

SECTION B - STATE AND CLASSIFICATION CONDITIONS

State amendatory endorsements, statutory benefit provisions, and assigned-risk rules apply before any conflicting general condition in this policy packet.

A classification shown on a schedule is not a warranty that all operations at the insured location are limited to that class.

Officer, partner, member, volunteer, leased-worker, and subcontractor treatment is determined by the attached endorsements and the applicable state rules.

Certificates from subcontractors must be available for audit and must identify the period of work, covered operations, and limits carried by the subcontractor.

Blue Kettle Food Service, LLC                                                             WC 00 00 00 C
